# Onion Routing Course — Full Claims Ledger

**Machine-readable companion:** `claims-ledger.json` (same data, all fields per claim).
**Adjudicated problems only:** `FINAL_REPORT.md` / `CHECKLIST.md`.

## What this is
Every atomic factual claim extracted from the course in Phase 1 of the 2026-06-21 technical-accuracy audit, with the verdict and the BOLT primary-source evidence used to check it. Purpose: let a future agent re-verify quickly (diff against current code) instead of re-auditing from scratch.

## How to use / caveats
- **`location` = `file:line` at audit time.** Line numbers drift as code changes — the **`quote` text is the durable anchor**; re-locate by quote, not line.
- Primary sources are the BOLT files staged alongside this audit (`bolt04.md`, `bolt07.md`, `01-messaging.md`, `02-peer-protocol.md`, `03-transactions.md`, `onion-test.json`, `onion-error-test.json`).
- Verdicts are the **Phase-1 first-pass** assessment. 71 problems were then adversarially re-verified; **8 were cleared as false positives** (marked `⚠ CLEARED` below). The adjudicated problem list is in `FINAL_REPORT.md`.
- `needsAdversarialCheck=true` marks claims the auditor wanted an independent skeptic to re-check.

|---|---|
| Correct | 957 |
| Incorrect | 35 |

### chapter 1.0-a-lightning-payment  ·  11 claims · 1 flagged

Extracted every factual/technical assertion in the prose. Per instructions, did NOT audit the embedded visual components (<lightning-network>, <htlc-propagation>) or their hover diagrams, nor checkpoints (none present) — those are covered by other agents. Verified prose claims against staged primary sources: BOLT 3 (/tmp/onion-audit/03-transactions.md: fun

- **C11** `client/public/onion_routing_tutorial/1.0-a-lightning-payment.md:18` · glossary · ❌ INCORRECT **[Low]**
    - claim: "immedieately"
    - evidence: Spelling typo in rendered prose a student reads. Should be 'immediately'. Technical content is unaffected — Low severity, not a protocol error.
    - should be: immediately
- **C3** `client/public/onion_routing_tutorial/1.0-a-lightning-payment.md:18` · formula · ✓ acceptable
    - claim: "the local party's output is always delayed, and the remote's is always immedieately spendable"
    - evidence: BOLT 3 L104 + L113-124: to_local is CSV-delayed by to_self_delay (correct). L136-146: to_remote is a simple P2WPKH (immediately spendable) WITHOUT option_anchors, but L138 adds a 1-block CSV WITH option_anchors. Course teaches the legacy/non-anchor model (consistent with Course 1), so 'immediately spendable' is a valid
- **C5** `client/public/onion_routing_tutorial/1.0-a-lightning-payment.md:20` · numeric · ✓ acceptable
    - claim: "watch a 10,000-sat payment travel through the network"
    - evidence: Sats-not-msat is a declared intended simplification. 10,000 sats is the single concrete amount in this chapter's prose; no fees/CLTV arithmetic stated in prose, so nothing to cross-check internally here. Downstream drift check: any other chapter/visual stating the headline amount should match 10,000 sats.
- **C8** `client/public/onion_routing_tutorial/1.0-a-lightning-payment.md:20` · checkpoint · ✓ acceptable
    - claim: "When the preimage propagates back, the HTLC unwinds and the sats move into the recipient's to_local"
    - evidence: BOLT 2 L2600-2601: on receiving update_fulfill_htlc (preimage) for an outgoing HTLC, fulfill the incoming HTLC — i.e. the preimage propagates backward (Dave→Charlie→Bob→Alice). On fulfillment the HTLC output is removed and its value is added to the claiming party's balance. On that party's OWN commitment tx the balance
- **C1** `client/public/onion_routing_tutorial/1.0-a-lightning-payment.md:10` · consistency · ✅ correct
    - claim: "Bob has a channel with both Alice and Charlie, and Charlie has a channel with both Bob and Dave. So the payment travels Alice → Bob → Charlie → Dave"
    - evidence: Topology is internally consistent and defines the canonical 3-hop main path. Characters are only Alice/Bob/Charlie/Dave as required. Adjacencies stated (Bob~Alice, Bob~Charlie, Charlie~Bob, Charlie~Dave) exactly support the path Alice→Bob→Charlie→Dave.
- **C2** `client/public/onion_routing_tutorial/1.0-a-lightning-payment.md:18` · checkpoint · ✅ correct
    - claim: "every Lightning channel is anchored by a pair of commitment transactions, one held by each channel partner. The input to both commitment transactions is the Funding UTXO, which locks the channel balance to a shared 2-of-2 multisig."
    - evidence: BOLT 3 /tmp/onion-audit/03-transactions.md:77-81 funding output is P2WSH to `2 <pubkey1> <pubkey2> 2 OP_CHECKMULTISIG` (2-of-2). L87-91 each commitment tx has txin[0] = the funding outpoint. Each side holds its own commitment tx (mirror pair).
- **C4** `client/public/onion_routing_tutorial/1.0-a-lightning-payment.md:18` · checkpoint · ✅ correct
    - claim: "this asymmetric delay ensures that, if one party attempts to cheat by publishing an old state, their counterparty has time to sweep all of their funds."
    - evidence: BOLT 3 L104: outputs returning funds to the commitment owner are delayed for to_self_delay 'to allow an opportunity for penalty transactions, in case of a revoked commitment transaction.' L115: to_local can be claimed without delay by the other party if they know the revocation private key. Matches the prose.
- **C6** `client/public/onion_routing_tutorial/1.0-a-lightning-payment.md:20` · checkpoint · ✅ correct
    - claim: "an HTLC output appears, locked to the same payment hash and a decrementing expiry locktime"
    - evidence: BOLT 2 L2788 HTLC carries payment_hash; same payment_hash used across the route (L2856 allows multiple HTLCs with same payment_hash). BOLT 4 L322 outgoing_cltv_value = cltv_expiry - cltv_expiry_delta, so the CLTV (expiry locktime) decrements at each hop going downstream. 'Same payment hash' + 'decrementing expiry' both
- **C7** `client/public/onion_routing_tutorial/1.0-a-lightning-payment.md:20` · checkpoint · ✅ correct
    - claim: "the timelock must expire at the last node in the payment path first, as this helps ensure that the payment will not partially succeed or fail"
    - evidence: BOLT 4 L322/L337: outgoing_cltv_value = cltv_expiry - cltv_expiry_delta — expiries DECREASE downstream, so the final hop (Dave) has the smallest/earliest expiry block height and times out FIRST. BOLT 2 L2616-2664 rationale: the downstream HTLC must resolve before the upstream one so a forwarder is never stuck with its 
- **C9** `client/public/onion_routing_tutorial/1.0-a-lightning-payment.md:20` · consistency · ✅ correct
    - claim: "Bob and Charlie each hold two commitment transactions, one for each of their payment channels."
    - evidence: Per the topology in L10: Bob has 2 channels (Alice, Charlie) and Charlie has 2 channels (Bob, Dave). In each channel a node holds its own commitment tx, so Bob and Charlie each hold 2. Alice (1 channel) and Dave (1 channel) hold 1 each — consistent; prose correctly highlights only Bob and Charlie.
- **C10** `client/public/onion_routing_tutorial/1.0-a-lightning-payment.md:22` · consistency · ✅ correct
    - claim: "Hover any commitment to inspect the full BOLT 3 transaction."
    - evidence: Commitment transactions are specified in BOLT 3 (/tmp/onion-audit/03-transactions.md 'Commitment Transaction' L83). The reference is accurate; the actual hover content is a visual-component concern out of scope for this prose audit.

Verified every factual claim against staged primary sources: BOLT 4 (/tmp/onion-audit/bolt04.md — Onion Decryption reader requirements L917-966, Accepting/Forwarding L643-711, Failure Messages L1280-1538, payload TLV format L188-219, max_htlc_cltv L1775-1778, packet structure/1366B L137-162/782), BOLT 7 (/tmp/onion-audit/bolt07.md — HTLC fee formula L981, ch

- **C12** `10.0-forwarding-validation.md:41` · code · ⚠ MISLEADING **[Low]**
    - claim: "when the channel was opened, Charlie set the smallest HTLC he'd accept"
    - evidence: BOLT7 bolt07.md:522 htlc_minimum_msat is advertised in channel_update and can be revised after opening, not fixed 'when the channel was opened'. Direction/ownership claim (Charlie's minimum) is correct; the temporal 'when the channel was opened' is an over-precise simplification.
    - should be: Charlie advertises the smallest HTLC he'll accept in his channel_update for that direction (it can be updated, not fixed at channel open).
- **C13** `10.0-forwarding-validation.md:45` · numeric · ❓ UNVERIFIABLE **[Low]**
    - claim: "LDK fails back any HTLC within 39 blocks (about six and a half hours) of expiry, a number built from the same reorg-and-confirmation math BOLT 2 uses to recommend the 34-block cltv_expiry_delta."
    - evidence: 39 blocks * 10 min = 390 min = 6.5 hours (internally correct). BOLT2 02-peer-protocol.md:2690-2691 confirms 'cltv_expiry_delta of at least 34 is reasonable (R=2,G=2,S=12)' from 3R+2G+2S reorg math. The specific LDK '39 blocks' figure is an external implementation claim not in staged BOLT sources; attributed to LDK, pla
- **C8** `10.0-forwarding-validation.md:29` · consistency · ✓ acceptable
    - claim: "What if both are present? Then the payment is malformed ... If neither are there, it's also malformed!"
    - evidence: BOLT4 bolt04.md:282-285: non-final MUST include scid + MUST NOT include payment_data; final MUST NOT include scid. A payload with both, or neither (no scid and no amt/cltv), violates the MUST/MUST NOT structure and a reader rejects (invalid_onion_payload). Spec doesn't phrase it as 'both/neither malformed' but the simp
- **C1** `10.0-forwarding-validation.md:11` · numeric · ✅ correct
    - claim: "If the packet isn't 1,366 bytes or the version byte isn't 0x00, Bob rejects it immediately. ... the only currently acceptable version is 0x00 and the length must be 1,366."
    - evidence: BOLT4 bolt04.md:782 'returns a single 1366-byte packet'; L162 'For this specification (version 0), version has a constant value of 0x00'; L40-43 higher-version packet MUST be discarded. Reader requirements L918-919 check version!=0 first.
- **C2** `10.0-forwarding-validation.md:12` · crypto · ✅ correct
    - claim: "Bob recomputes HMAC-SHA256(mu_i, hop_payloads || associated_data) with his own mu key and compares it against the hmac field ... rejects them with invalid_onion_hmac."
    - evidence: BOLT4 bolt04.md:935-939 'Derive mu as HMAC256("mu",ss)'; 'Derive the HMAC as HMAC256(mu, hop_payloads || associated_data)'; 'MUST use a constant time comparison ... If ... differ: MUST abort'. Failure code L1516-1517 invalid_onion_hmac.
- **C3** `10.0-forwarding-validation.md:9-13` · crypto · ✅ correct
    - claim: "verify, then peel ... HMAC verification (the integrity check). Next ... Peel. If the HMAC verifies, then Bob decrypts the onion ... He derives rho, XORs the extended keystream"
    - evidence: BOLT4 Onion Decryption reader order bolt04.md:934-942: derive mu -> compute HMAC -> constant-time compare -> abort if differ -> THEN derive rho -> XOR. HMAC is verified strictly before rho-decrypt. Matches chapter's FOCUS claim (verify HMAC BEFORE decrypt).
- **C4** `10.0-forwarding-validation.md:13` · crypto · ✅ correct
    - claim: "He derives rho, XORs the extended keystream across the buffer, and lifts his hop payload off the front."
    - evidence: BOLT4 bolt04.md:940-949: derive rho, derive bytestream twice length of hop_payloads, XOR, remove bigsize length then payload_length bytes from front as payload.
- **C5** `10.0-forwarding-validation.md:14` · code · ✅ correct
    - claim: "is there a short_channel_id? If so, then he's a forwarder ... If there is payment_data and no short_channel_id, then Bob is the destination"
    - evidence: BOLT4 bolt04.md:282-285 non-final MUST include short_channel_id & MUST NOT include payment_data; final MUST NOT include short_channel_id & includes payment_data if secret provided.
- **C6** `10.0-forwarding-validation.md:24-27` · code · ✅ correct
    - claim: "Type 2: amt_to_forward (msat). Type 4: outgoing_cltv_value (block height). Type 6: short_channel_id ... Type 8: payment_data (final hop only): payment_secret + total_msat."
    - evidence: BOLT4 payload format bolt04.md:194-206: type2 amt_to_forward tu64; type4 outgoing_cltv_value tu32; type6 short_channel_id; type8 payment_data = [32*byte payment_secret][tu64 total_msat].
- **C7** `10.0-forwarding-validation.md:29` · code · ✅ correct
    - claim: "Bob will read the TLV records in order (their type numbers have to increase as he goes)."
    - evidence: BOLT1 01-messaging.md:147 'MUST order tlv_records in a tlv_stream by strictly-increasing type'; L205 all types must appear in increasing order.
- **C9** `10.0-forwarding-validation.md:39` · formula · ✅ correct
    - claim: "Sufficient fee (fee_insufficient). The incoming amount must exceed amt_to_forward by at least Bob's advertised fee (fee_base_msat plus fee_proportional_millionths)."
    - evidence: BOLT4 bolt04.md:336 fails if incoming amount_msat - fee < amt_to_forward, i.e. incoming - amt_to_forward >= fee. Failure code fee_insufficient (bolt04.md:1495-1498). Prose's 'fee_base plus fee_proportional' is loose but the actual product/floor is shown in snippet C16.
- **C10** `10.0-forwarding-validation.md:40` · formula · ✅ correct
    - claim: "Enough CLTV cushion (incorrect_cltv_expiry). The incoming CLTV must exceed outgoing_cltv_value by at least Bob's advertised cltv_expiry_delta"
    - evidence: BOLT4 bolt04.md:337 fails if cltv_expiry - cltv_expiry_delta < outgoing_cltv_value, i.e. cltv_expiry - outgoing_cltv_value >= cltv_expiry_delta; L1349-1353 incorrect_cltv_expiry requires cltv_expiry - cltv_expiry_delta >= outgoing_cltv_value.
- **C11** `10.0-forwarding-validation.md:41` · code · ✅ correct ⚠ CLEARED on re-verify (false positive — no change needed)
    - claim: "Above the channel minimum (amount_below_minimum). amt_to_forward must be at least the outgoing channel's htlc_minimum_msat. Whose minimum? Charlie's"
    - evidence: BOLT4 bolt04.md:1491-1494 forwarder fails amount_below_minimum if HTLC amount < currently specified minimum for the OUTGOING channel. BOLT7 bolt07.md:522-523 htlc_minimum_msat = minimum the channel PEER will accept (the receiving peer = Charlie on Bob->Charlie). The outgoing HTLC carries amt_to_forward.
- **C14** `10.0-forwarding-validation.md:46` · numeric · ✅ correct
    - claim: "every major implementation enforces a standard of 2,016 blocks, about two weeks, so BOLT 4 eventually pinned max_htlc_cltv at exactly that."
    - evidence: BOLT4 bolt04.md:1777 'This max_htlc_cltv value is defined as 2016 blocks, based on historical value deployed by Lightning implementations.' 2016*10min=20160min=14 days = about two weeks.
- **C15** `10.0-forwarding-validation.md:45-46` · code · ✅ correct
    - claim: "expiry_too_soon ... BOLT 4 lets Bob reject a CLTV 'unreasonably near the present' ... expiry_too_far ... Bob MAY reject a CLTV more than his configured maximum"
    - evidence: BOLT4 bolt04.md:1504-1508: 'if the cltv_expiry is unreasonably near the present: return an expiry_too_soon error'; 'if the cltv_expiry is more than max_htlc_cltv in the future: return an expiry_too_far error'. Both under 'A forwarding node MAY'.
- **C16** `10.0-forwarding-validation.md:50 (snippet check-fee-cltv)` · formula · ✅ correct
    - claim: "required_fee = policy.fee_base_msat + (amt_to_forward * policy.fee_proportional_millionths) // 1_000_000 ; if incoming_amount_msat - amt_to_forward < required_fee: return 'fee_insufficient'"
    - evidence: BOLT7 bolt07.md:981 fee = fee_base_msat + (amount_to_forward * fee_proportional_millionths / 1000000) with integer (floored) division. Snippet floor-divides with // and the failure boundary matches BOLT4 L336 (exact fee passes). PythonSnippet.tsx:189.
- **C17** `10.0-forwarding-validation.md:52` · consistency · ✅ correct
    - claim: "It isn't the Route C policy from chapter 2 (where Bob's delta was 20)."
    - evidence: ForwarderPolicyMap.tsx:114 Route C Bob->Charlie cltvDelta:20. The standalone ch10 exercise uses cltv_expiry_delta=40 (onion-routing-exercises-draft.ts:547); the note correctly distinguishes them. Internally consistent.
- **C18** `10.0-forwarding-validation.md:40` · consistency · ✅ correct
    - claim: "jump back to the CLTV race-condition deep dive (/onion-routing-tutorial/pathfinding-101#cltv-race-condition) at the bottom of chapter 2."
    - evidence: Anchor exists: 2.0-pathfinding-101.md:92 '<a id="cltv-race-condition"></a>'. Chapter slug 'pathfinding-101' confirmed in onion-routing-tutorial.tsx:444/448. Cross-reference resolves.
- **C19** `10.0-forwarding-validation.md:57` · code · ✅ correct
    - claim: "If Bob's downstream channel is offline or has insufficient liquidity, then he will fail the HTLC with temporary_channel_failure."
    - evidence: BOLT4 bolt04.md:1478-1482 'A forwarding node MAY ... if during forwarding ... a transient error occurs in the outgoing channel (e.g. channel capacity reached, too many in-flight HTLCs, etc.): return a temporary_channel_failure error.'
- **C20** `10.0-forwarding-validation.md:69-71` · code · ✅ correct
    - claim: "Forward (short_channel_id present): send the peeled next_packet ... with amt_to_forward as the amount and outgoing_cltv_value as the timelock. ... Reject ... builds an error onion using the appropriate failure code and his um key."
    - evidence: BOLT4 forward uses amt_to_forward/outgoing_cltv_value (bolt04.md:223-235). um key 'used during error reporting' (bolt04.md:112). Error-onion construction with um covered in ch11.
- **C21** `10.0-forwarding-validation.md:77` · code · ✅ correct
    - claim: "verify_hmac ... compute the HMAC-SHA256 over the inbound hop_payloads || associated_data with the forwarder's mu key and compare ... returning True or False."
    - evidence: Matches exercise exercise-verify-hmac-draft (onion-routing-exercises-draft.ts:404-405): recompute HMAC-SHA256(mu, hop_payloads || associated_data), compare packet[1334:1366], return bool via hmac.compare_digest.
- **C22** `10.0-forwarding-validation.md:79-83` · code · ✅ correct
    - claim: "check_forward ... validate two things: 1) incoming amount covers amt_to_forward plus Bob's fee (else fee_insufficient) 2) incoming CLTV clears outgoing_cltv_value by at least his delta (else incorrect_cltv_expiry). This function returns the BOLT 4 failure code, or nothing if the "
    - evidence: Matches exercise exercise-check-forward-draft (onion-routing-exercises-draft.ts:505-539): returns str|None; fee_insufficient and incorrect_cltv_expiry codes; fee check run first. Return None when safe.
- **C23** `10.0-forwarding-validation.md:5` · code · ✅ correct

    - evidence: BOLT7 bolt07.md:520-528 channel_update sets cltv_expiry_delta, htlc_minimum_msat, fee_base_msat, fee_proportional_millionths. BOLT2 contains HTLC forwarding requirements (link valid).

### chapter 11.0-error-onion  ·  27 claims · all clean
_Coverage:_ Audited the full prose of /Users/austinv2/code/onion-routing/client/public/onion_routing_tutorial/11.0-error-onion.md (115 lines). Verified every factual/numeric/crypto assertion against the staged primary sources: BOLT 4 error-onion section (/tmp/onion-audit/bolt04.md lines 1038-1267: Erring node return-packet layout, um/ammag key gen, pad>=256 rule, intermediate XOR re-wrap, origin iterative decrypt), BOLT 4 worked Returning-Errors trace (lines 1782-1854, 5-hop, failure node 4), the simpler er

- **C11** `client/public/onion_routing_tutorial/11.0-error-onion.md:40` · formula · ✓ acceptable
    - claim: "what about failure messages *bigger* than 256 bytes... Those get padded to a bigger fixed total instead."
    - evidence: BOLT4 bolt04.md:1134-1137 mandates only failure_len+pad_len>=256 (SHOULD be exactly 256). There is no spec-mandated 'fixed' larger total for big messages; it is implementation/test-vector convention. The word 'fixed' slightly over-states the spec, but the chapter immediately anchors it to the test vector (which is corr
- **C25** `client/public/onion_routing_tutorial/11.0-error-onion.md:58` · formula · ✓ acceptable
    - claim: "he sends `wrapped` back to Bob, his upstream hop, as the failure data on the HTLC."
    - evidence: BOLT4 bolt04.md:1147 stores the wrapped bytes as the `reason` field of update_fail_htlc/update_htlc_fail. The chapter abstracts this as 'failure data on the HTLC' — substantively correct, consistent with the course's level of wire-message abstraction. Upstream peer = Bob, correct.
- **C1** `client/public/onion_routing_tutorial/11.0-error-onion.md:9` · crypto · ✅ correct
    - claim: "When a hop decides to fail a payment, it authenticates the failure message with its `um` key, encrypts it with its `ammag` keystream, and then hands it to its *upstream* peer."
    - evidence: BOLT4 /tmp/onion-audit/bolt04.md:1066-1072 — return packet hmac uses key type `um`; erring node then generates `ammag` key and XORs the packet. Upstream = toward sender (Alice); Charlie's upstream peer is Bob. Order (auth then encrypt) matches spec.
- **C2** `client/public/onion_routing_tutorial/11.0-error-onion.md:9` · crypto · ✅ correct
    - claim: "As each upstream hop receives the message, it will add one more `ammag` layer of encryption and pass it along."
    - evidence: BOLT4 bolt04.md:1146-1149,1188 — every intermediate node generates its `ammag` key and XORs (obfuscation step identical to erring node), then MUST return-forward.
- **C3** `client/public/onion_routing_tutorial/11.0-error-onion.md:11` · crypto · ✅ correct
    - claim: "Alice doesn't know which hop the error came from, so she finds out by trial and error: peel a layer with Bob's `ammag`, check the result against Bob's `um` HMAC. If there is no match, then she tries again with Charlie's key... Whichever hop's keys produce a valid HMAC, that's the"
    - evidence: BOLT4 bolt04.md:1198,1223-1226 — origin iteratively decrypts with each hop's ammag, computes HMAC with hop's um; when it matches `hmac`, that hop is the sender of the failure. Peel order most-recent-first (Bob then Charlie) is required for the HMAC to verify at the correct position.
- **C4** `client/public/onion_routing_tutorial/11.0-error-onion.md:15` · crypto · ✅ correct
    - claim: "Alice can trust the error... that it wasn't forged or modified along the way back. Why? Because only the failing hop knows its own `um` key."
    - evidence: um is derived from the Alice-Charlie shared secret (bolt04.md:111,119-122 key type `um`=0x756d over ss). Only Alice and Charlie hold ss_AC, so a valid um_charlie HMAC authenticates Charlie as author; no intermediate (Bob) can forge it. From Alice's verifier standpoint the claim holds.
- **C5** `client/public/onion_routing_tutorial/11.0-error-onion.md:16` · crypto · ✅ correct
    - claim: "The hops between the failing one and Alice can't read what the error says, or even tell where it originated. Each hop only knows its own `ammag` and `um` keys, not anyone else's."
    - evidence: Bob receives error XORed under ammag_charlie which he lacks, so he cannot decrypt (bolt04.md:1146-1149 intermediate only re-XORs, never reads). Bob knows the error arrived from his downstream peer Charlie's direction but cannot determine the true origin hop (could be Charlie or any node beyond) — standard Sphinx proper
- **C6** `client/public/onion_routing_tutorial/11.0-error-onion.md:21` · crypto · ✅ correct
    - claim: "Re-wrapping at each hop means no two channels ever carry correlating bytes, the same property the forward onion gets from changing at every hop."
    - evidence: BOLT4 bolt04.md:1146-1149 — each hop applies its own ammag XOR so the bytes on each channel differ; this is the deliberate analogue of the forward onion's per-hop transformation. Rationale matches spec intent (untraceability).
- **C7** `client/public/onion_routing_tutorial/11.0-error-onion.md:30` · formula · ✅ correct
    - claim: "Charlie constructs the failure message: the failure code plus any associated data (like a `channel_update` for `UPDATE`-flagged failures)."
    - evidence: BOLT4 bolt04.md:1251-1253 failuremsg = 2-byte failure_code + type data; bolt04.md:1269 `0x1000 (UPDATE)`; bolt04.md:1303-1347 UPDATE-flagged codes (temporary_channel_failure, fee_insufficient, incorrect_cltv_expiry...) each carry `[len*byte:channel_update]`.
- **C8** `client/public/onion_routing_tutorial/11.0-error-onion.md:33-38` · numeric · ✅ correct
    - claim: "he writes four pieces, one after another (260 bytes total in our example): `failure_len` (2 bytes)... the `failure_message` itself (`failure_len` bytes)... `pad_len` (2 bytes)... the padding itself (`pad_len` bytes)."
    - evidence: BOLT4 bolt04.md:1059-1064 return packet = [32:hmac][u16:failure_len][failure_len:failuremsg][u16:pad_len][pad_len:pad]. The 4 post-HMAC fields match. Simpler vector onion-error-test.json hop[4].payload decodes (Python) to 260 bytes: failure_len=2, msg=2002, pad_len=254, total 2+2+2+254=260.
- **C9** `client/public/onion_routing_tutorial/11.0-error-onion.md:38` · crypto · ✅ correct
    - claim: "BOLT 4 only constrains the *length* of the pad, not its contents, but senders conventionally zero-fill it (and the spec's own test vector uses `0x00` bytes)"
    - evidence: BOLT4 bolt04.md:1134-1135 only constrains failure_len+pad_len length, says nothing about pad contents. onion-error-test.json hop[4].payload pad bytes are all 0x00 (254 zero bytes verified in Python). Worked example payload (bolt04.md:1817) pad is also 0x00.
- **C10** `client/public/onion_routing_tutorial/11.0-error-onion.md:40` · numeric · ✅ correct
    - claim: "Per BOLT 4, `failure_len + pad_len` must come to at least 256... and the two length fields bring the total to 260."
    - evidence: BOLT4 bolt04.md:1134 'MUST set `pad` such that the `failure_len` plus `pad_len` is at least 256'. In the 260-byte example: failure_len+pad_len=256, plus the two 2-byte length fields = 260. Confirmed by onion-error-test.json decode (256+4=260).
- **C12** `client/public/onion_routing_tutorial/11.0-error-onion.md:40` · numeric · ✅ correct
    - claim: "In fact, the spec's own test vector pads to 1,024 bytes, making a 1,060-byte packet!"
    - evidence: Python decode of BOLT4 bolt04.md:1817 payload: failure_len=320, pad_len=704, failure_len+pad_len=1024, payload total=1028 bytes; raw_error_packet (bolt04.md:1819) = 1060 bytes (= 32-byte HMAC + 1028). Both numbers exact.
- **C13** `client/public/onion_routing_tutorial/11.0-error-onion.md:45` · crypto · ✅ correct
    - claim: "Charlie computes an HMAC over the 260-byte payload with his `um` key: `error_hmac = HMAC-SHA256(um_charlie, payload)`."
    - evidence: BOLT4 bolt04.md:1066-1067 hmac authenticates the remainder of the packet with key type `um`; key gen uses SHA256 (bolt04.md:119). HMAC covers the payload (everything after the 32-byte hmac). Matches snippet error-hmac (PythonSnippet.tsx:167 hmac.new(um_charlie, payload, hashlib.sha256)).
- **C14** `client/public/onion_routing_tutorial/11.0-error-onion.md:48` · numeric · ✅ correct
    - claim: "he prepends the HMAC to the payload: `error_hmac (32 bytes) || payload (260 bytes)`. That's the full error packet, 292 bytes in all for our example."
    - evidence: BOLT4 bolt04.md:1059-1060 [32*byte:hmac] is the first field. 32 + 260 = 292. Arithmetic correct; field order (hmac first) matches spec.
- **C15** `client/public/onion_routing_tutorial/11.0-error-onion.md:53` · crypto · ✅ correct
    - claim: "he encrypts the whole packet by XOR-ing it with his `ammag` keystream: `wrapped = error_packet ⊕ ChaCha20(ammag_charlie, len(error_packet))`."
    - evidence: BOLT4 bolt04.md:1070-1072 — erring node generates `ammag` key, generates a pseudo-random stream (ChaCha20, bolt04.md:131-133), applies to the packet using XOR. Whole-packet XOR over its full length. Matches snippet error-wrap.
- **C16** `client/public/onion_routing_tutorial/11.0-error-onion.md:64` · crypto · ✅ correct
    - claim: "When Bob receives the error onion... he doesn't know what's inside (he doesn't have Charlie's `ammag` key), and BOLT 4 says he doesn't need to. His only job is to wrap one more layer: `wrapped = wrapped ⊕ ChaCha20(ammag_bob, len(wrapped))`."
    - evidence: BOLT4 bolt04.md:1146-1149 intermediate node only generates ammag key and XORs ('obfuscation step identical to the erring node'); it never decrypts/reads. XOR over however-many bytes arrived (fixed size, no re-padding). Matches snippet error-rewrap.
- **C17** `client/public/onion_routing_tutorial/11.0-error-onion.md:68` · crypto · ✅ correct
    - claim: "If there were more hops between Alice and Charlie (say, a 5-hop route), each one would wrap with its own `ammag` in turn. By the time the error reaches Alice, it's been XORed with every intermediate hop's keystream plus the originating Charlie's keystream."
    - evidence: BOLT4 bolt04.md:1187-1189 all intermediate nodes MUST transform (XOR) and return-forward. The wire bytes Alice receives = error XORed by Charlie then each intermediate in turn. Matches the spec's 5-hop worked trace (bolt04.md:1821-1853 successive ammag XOR stages).
- **C18** `client/public/onion_routing_tutorial/11.0-error-onion.md:72` · consistency · ✅ correct
    - claim: "Alice... has shared secrets ss_AB, ss_AC, ss_AD (one per hop) and can derive the corresponding `um` and `ammag` keys for each."
    - evidence: Main path Alice->Bob->Charlie->Dave (1.0-a-lightning-payment.md:10). Alice shares a secret with each of Bob/Charlie/Dave; she precomputes um+ammag for all because she does not know which hop will fail. BOLT4 bolt04.md:1195-1196 origin 'generates the ammag, ammagext and um keys for each hop in the route.' Listing all th
- **C19** `client/public/onion_routing_tutorial/11.0-error-onion.md:77` · crypto · ✅ correct
    - claim: "Check whether the leading 32 bytes are a valid HMAC over the rest under that hop's `um` key, i.e. whether `HMAC-SHA256(um_i, wrapped[32:])` equals `wrapped[:32]`."
    - evidence: BOLT4 bolt04.md:1223-1225 compute HMAC for return packet with hop's um; when it matches `hmac` (the leading 32 bytes), that hop is the failure source. wrapped[:32]=hmac, wrapped[32:]=authenticated payload. Matches snippet error-trial-peel.
- **C20** `client/public/onion_routing_tutorial/11.0-error-onion.md:81` · crypto · ✅ correct
    - claim: "The wrapping order from the network's perspective is: Charlie XORs first, then Bob XORs... the *outermost* layer is the most recent hop's wrap (Bob's...), and the *innermost* is Charlie's (the failing hop). Alice peels in the order Bob → Charlie, which is `i = 0, 1, ...` since ho"
    - evidence: Charlie wraps first (bolt04.md:1070-1072), Bob wraps last before Alice (bolt04.md:1146). To verify Charlie's HMAC, Alice must remove exactly Bob's layer then Charlie's, leaving `error`. Peeling order (most-recent/outermost Bob=i0 first, then Charlie=i1) is required: peeling Charlie first would leave error XOR ammag_bob
- **C21** `client/public/onion_routing_tutorial/11.0-error-onion.md:87` · crypto · ✅ correct
    - claim: "What if she peels through every layer and never finds a valid HMAC? Then the error packet is malformed, which means someone along the return path tampered with it (or sent garbage)."
    - evidence: If no hop's um verifies, the origin cannot attribute the failure (BOLT4 bolt04.md:1239 'When the failure source cannot be identified from the return packet'). Implies corruption/tampering on the return path. Accurate.
- **C22** `client/public/onion_routing_tutorial/11.0-error-onion.md:95` · crypto · ✅ correct
    - claim: "First, Charlie builds: `error = HMAC(um_charlie, padded_msg) || padded_msg`. Then he wraps: `wire = error ⊕ ammag_charlie_stream` and sends `wire` back to Bob."
    - evidence: BOLT4 bolt04.md:1059-1072: hmac (over remainder) prepended to packet, then ammag XOR. padded_msg = failure_len||failuremsg||pad_len||pad. Charlie's upstream peer is Bob (Alice->Bob->Charlie). Consistent with C1/C13/C15.
- **C23** `client/public/onion_routing_tutorial/11.0-error-onion.md:100-101` · crypto · ✅ correct
    - claim: "Iteration i=0 (Bob's keys): `peeled = wire ⊕ ammag_bob_stream`. ... Bob isn't the failing hop, so his `um` won't authenticate... Iteration i=1 (Charlie's keys): `peeled = peeled ⊕ ammag_charlie_stream`. Now `peeled` is exactly Charlie's original `error` packet, so the HMAC check "
    - evidence: wire = error XOR ammag_charlie XOR ammag_bob. i=0 removes ammag_bob -> error XOR ammag_charlie (Bob um fails). i=1 removes ammag_charlie -> error (Charlie um verifies). In `error`: bytes [0:32]=hmac, [32:34]=failure_len, [34:]=failuremsg. Slicing exact. Matches snippet error-parse (which reads payload[0:2]/payload[2:] 
- **C24** `client/public/onion_routing_tutorial/11.0-error-onion.md:103` · crypto · ✅ correct
    - claim: "the failing hop is identified by **whose `um` key verifies**, which Alice checks by trial-and-decrypt as she peels."
    - evidence: BOLT4 bolt04.md:1223-1226 — the hop whose um produces a matching HMAC is the sender of the failure. Restates C3/C19 accurately.
- **C26** `client/public/onion_routing_tutorial/11.0-error-onion.md:3` · glossary · ✅ correct
    - claim: "a node might be offline, a channel might lack liquidity, a CLTV might be too tight, or an invoice might have expired."
    - evidence: Illustrative, maps to real failure codes: temporary_node_failure (offline), temporary_channel_failure (liquidity), incorrect_cltv_expiry/expiry_too_soon (tight CLTV), incorrect_or_unknown_payment_details (expired invoice). No precise code claim made; all plausible.
- **C27** `client/public/onion_routing_tutorial/11.0-error-onion.md:3-115` · consistency · ✅ correct
    - claim: "(whole chapter) — no payment_hash field is stated to be present in the error/failure message."
    - evidence: Failure messages (BOLT4 bolt04.md:1251-1463) carry failure_code + type-specific fields (sha256_of_onion, channel_update, htlc_msat, etc.) but never a payment_hash.     - evidence: Not a BOLT claim; well-known about LND/CLN/LDK/Eclair pathfinding (Dijkstra/modified-Dijkstra variants weighting fee + success probability). BOLT 7 bolt07.md:1029-1054 'Recommendations for Routing' frames fee vs cltv tradeoff. General/accurate.

    - evidence: Consistent with C10 and BOLT 7 Recommendations-for-Routing rationale (bolt07.md:1031-1035). The incoming HTLC expires cltv_expiry_delta blocks AFTER the outgoing, giving the forwarder a window to claim incoming after learning the preimage from the resolved outgoing.

    - evidence: Final hop has smallest cltv_expiry (e.g. 168) and each upstream HTLC larger (183, 203 / 1168), i.e. expires later.     - evidence: Trace: Charlie learns preimage only by paying Dave (Dave claims Charlie->Dave HTLC, so Dave is paid). - **C1** `4.0-shared-secrets.md:10` · crypto · ✅ correct
    - claim: "a public key is just a large, private number multiplied by the elliptic curve generator point: `A = a · G`"
    - evidence: BOLT4:498 `E_0 = e_0 \cdot G`; standard secp256k1 pubkey = privkey·G. Chapter's lowercase=private/uppercase=public convention matches BOLT usage.
- **C2** `4.0-shared-secrets.md:10` · crypto · ✅ correct
    - claim: "you cannot recover `a` from `A` ... you'd have to solve the **elliptic curve discrete log problem**, which is computationally infeasible"
    - evidence: Standard ECDLP hardness assumption underlying secp256k1 (BOLT4:82 specifies secp256k1). Accurate.
- **C3** `4.0-shared-secrets.md:12` · crypto · ✅ correct
    - claim: "scalar multiplication on the curve is **commutative** ... given Alice's keypair `(a, A)` and Bob's `(b, B)`, the point `a · B` equals `b · A`, because both expand to `ab · G`"
    - evidence: a·B=a·(b·G)=ab·G and b·A=b·(a·G)=ab·G. BOLT4:739 uses the same phrasing 'Due to the commutative property of scalar multiplication'. The integer 3·5=5·3 analogy is correct.
- **C4** `4.0-shared-secrets.md:12` · crypto · ✅ correct
    - claim: "If Alice and Bob take the SHA256 hash of this point (serialized in its compressed 33-byte form, matching BOLT 4), they end up with a **shared secret**"
    - evidence: BOLT4:717-719 'resulting curve point is serialized to the compressed format and hashed using SHA256. The hash output is used as the 32-byte shared secret.' BOLT4:142 '33-byte compressed secp256k1 public_key'. BOLT4:745 'serialized in its compressed format'.
- **C6** `4.0-shared-secrets.md:22` · crypto · ✅ correct
    - claim: "Then she'd embed her own node public key at the top of the packet. Each forwarder reads it, performs ECDH between their own node's private key and that public key, and derives the same shared secret"
    - evidence: Strawman first attempt (node-key reuse). Mechanically valid ECDH. The pedagogical point — reusing the identity-tied node key leaks Alice's identity — matches BOLT4:32-33 'Each hop ... only sees an ephemeral key for the origin node, in order to hide the sender's identity.' Chapter line 32 draws the correct lesson.
- **C8** `4.0-shared-secrets.md:60` · crypto · ✅ correct
    - claim: "Alice will generate just **one** random private key, called the **session key** ... only the *first* ephemeral key ever needs to be embedded in the packet. For every subsequent hop, the *next* hop's ephemeral key is computed on the fly by the current hop"
    - evidence: BOLT4:755 'generates a random 32-byte sessionkey'; BOLT4:762-763 'initializes the ephemeral private key for the first hop ek_1 to the sessionkey'; BOLT4:817 only 'the ephemeral pubkey for the first hop' is in the packet header; forwarders advance the chain. onion-test.json session_key=0x41*32 (single key). - **C9** `4.0-shared-secrets.md:69` · crypto · ✅ correct
    - claim: "Alice sets the ephemeral private key equal to the session key ... e_AB = sessionkey"
    - evidence: BOLT4:762-763 'initializes the ephemeral private key for the first hop ek_1 to the sessionkey'. Hop 0 (Bob) = first hop. Correct.
- **C10** `4.0-shared-secrets.md:70` · crypto · ✅ correct
    - claim: "E_AB = e_AB · G"
    - evidence: BOLT4:763-764 'derives ... the corresponding ephemeral public key epk_1 by multiplying with the secp256k1 base point.' G = base/generator point. Correct.
- **C11** `4.0-shared-secrets.md:71` · crypto · ✅ correct
    - claim: "ss_AB = SHA256(e_AB · B)"
    - evidence: BOLT4:501 ss_i = SHA256(e_i * N_i); BOLT4:768-770 ECDH with hop's public key + ephemeral private key, hashed SHA256. B = Bob's node pubkey. Correct.
- **C12** `4.0-shared-secrets.md:72` · formula · ✅ correct
    - claim: "bf_AB = SHA256(E_AB ‖ ss_AB)"
    - evidence: BOLT4:743-746 'SHA256 hash value of the concatenation of the public key serialized in its compressed format and the shared secret'; BOLT4:503 e_{i+1}=SHA256(E_i || ss_i)*e_i (the SHA256(E||ss) term is the blinding factor). ‖ = concatenation = BOLT's ||. Correct.
- **C13** `4.0-shared-secrets.md:75` · formula · ✅ correct
    - claim: "e_AC = bf_AB · e_AB (mod n, the curve's order, which keeps the result a valid private key)"
    - evidence: BOLT4:773-774 'ephemeral private key for the next hop ek_{k+1} ... multiplying the current ephemeral private key ek_k by the blinding factor'; BOLT4:503 e_{i+1}=SHA256(E_i||ss_i)*e_i. Private-key scalar arithmetic on secp256k1 is implicitly mod n (group order); the 'mod n' annotation is correct and pedagogically approp
- **C14** `4.0-shared-secrets.md:76` · crypto · ✅ correct

    - evidence: BOLT4:775-776 'ephemeral public key for the next hop epk_{k+1} is derived from the ephemeral private key ek_{k+1} by multiplying with the base point.' Equivalent to BOLT4:504 E_{i+1}=SHA256(E_i||ss_i)*E_i. Correct.
- **C15** `4.0-shared-secrets.md:84` · crypto · ✅ correct
    - claim: "No blinding factor for Dave: he's the final hop, so there's no successor that would need one."
    - evidence: BOLT4:765-776 advances ek_{k+1} only to feed the NEXT hop; the final hop has no next hop, so its blinding factor / next ephemeral key is unused. Correct.
- **C16** `4.0-shared-secrets.md:90` · crypto · ✅ correct
    - claim: "Alice was able to compute (E_AB, ss_AB, E_AC, ss_AC, E_AD, ss_AD) in advance, all from her session key. Now, she just needs to include E_AB into the start of the onion"
    - evidence: BOLT4:778-781 construction needs r ephemeral pubkeys + r shared secrets all derived from sessionkey; BOLT4:817 only the first hop's ephemeral pubkey is placed in the packet header. The 6-tuple (3 pubkeys + 3 secrets) for a 3-hop path is internally consistent. Correct.
- **C17** `4.0-shared-secrets.md:98` · crypto · ✅ correct

    - evidence: BOLT4:504 E_{i+1}=SHA256(E_i||ss_i)*E_i; BOLT4:737-741 blinding of a pubkey is scalar mult of the EC point by the 32-byte blinding factor. bf_AB=SHA256(E_AB||ss_AB). Correct.
- **C19** `4.0-shared-secrets.md:102` · crypto · ✅ correct

    - evidence: Final hop derives its shared secret via ECDH (ss_AD=SHA256(dave_priv·E_AD)) but does not need a blinding factor / next ephemeral key. Consistent with C15 and BOLT4 chain semantics.
- **C20** `4.0-shared-secrets.md:104` · crypto · ✅ correct

- **C21** `4.0-shared-secrets.md:46` · crypto · ✅ correct

    - evidence: Describes the naive attempt-2 design but the per-hop ECDH-then-decrypt mechanic matches BOLT4:724-728 forwarding side. Uses correct locked term 'hop payload'. Correct.
- **C22** `4.0-shared-secrets.md:32` · crypto · ✅ correct

- **C11** `5.0-onion-routing-101.md:39` · crypto · ✓ acceptable

- **C1** `5.0-onion-routing-101.md:5` · numeric · ✅ correct

    - evidence: BOLT 4 L782: 'The construction returns a single 1366-byte packet'. BOLT 2 L2790: '[1366*byte:onion_routing_packet]'. Decomposes 1+33+1300+32=1366.
- **C2** `5.0-onion-routing-101.md:5` · crypto · ✅ correct
    - claim: "each hop can derive its shared secret using one single ephemeral Diffie-Hellman operation"

- **C2b** `5.0-onion-routing-101.md:5` · crypto · ✅ correct
    - claim: "Sphinx ... fixes two problems they had: packet sizes leaking the route length, and header sizes growing with the route"
    - evidence: BOLT 4 L9-37 + filler section L971-982 (fixed 1300B padding hides route length); blinded ephemeral keys (L730-741) keep header constant-size regardless of route length. Accurate characterization of Sphinx's improvements.
- **C4** `5.0-onion-routing-101.md:15` · crypto · ✅ correct
    - claim: "Sphinx uses a stream cipher (specifically ChaCha20), which produces a deterministic stream of pseudo-random bytes given a key."
    - evidence: BOLT 4 L83 ('ChaCha20 is used to generate a [pseudo-random stream]') and L131-135 (ChaCha20 over a 0x00-byte stream with zero nonce; deterministic given key). Correct.
- **C5** `5.0-onion-routing-101.md:15-17` · crypto · ✅ correct
    - claim: "Alice and Bob can each use the same shared secret to independently generate the exact same keystream ... encrypt the message by simply XOR-ing the plaintext with the keystream, byte-by-byte ... Bob can then XOR the ciphertext with the same keystream to decrypt it"
    - evidence: BOLT 4 L940-942: derive rho from ss, derive bytestream from rho, set unwrapped = XOR(hop_payloads, bytestream). Stream-cipher XOR is its own inverse with the same keystream. Correct (the keystream key is rho, derived from ss; chapter abstracts rho away here, fixed in 'A small confession').
- **C6** `5.0-onion-routing-101.md:35` · numeric · ✅ correct
    - claim: "HEADER holds the version byte (currently 0x00) and a single ephemeral public key for the current hop."
    - evidence: BOLT 4 L157-162: [byte:version][point:public_key]; 'version has a constant value of 0x00'. Test vector onion.json L29 begins '0002eec7245d...' = 0x00 version then 33-byte compressed key (0x02 prefix). One ephemeral pubkey. Correct.
- **C7** `5.0-onion-routing-101.md:35` · crypto · ✅ correct
    - claim: "the forwarder combines it with its own node private key (via ECDH) to derive its shared secret with Alice"
    - evidence: BOLT 4 L726-727: 'during packet forwarding, the hop uses the ephemeral public key and its own node ID private key'. L934: ss = ECDH(public_key, node_privkey). Correct.
- **C8** `5.0-onion-routing-101.md:35` · crypto · ✅ correct
    - claim: "the hop advances this key with the blinding factor from chapter 4 and writes the next hop's ephemeral pubkey into the packet it sends on"
    - evidence: BOLT 4 L956-959: derive blinding_tweak = SHA256(public_key||ss); forward with public_key set to incoming public_key multiplied by blinding_tweak. Construction side L771-776 confirms multiply-by-blinding-factor advances the ephemeral key. Correct.
- **C9** `5.0-onion-routing-101.md:37` · numeric · ✅ correct
    - claim: "PAYLOAD AREA carries one hop payload per hop, each holding a short length prefix ... the encrypted routing instructions (amount, CLTV, the next hop, etc.), and a 32-byte HMAC that the next hop will check."
    - evidence: BOLT 4 L167-172: hop_payloads = [bigsize:length][length:payload][32:hmac] repeated. Payload TLV types: 2=amt_to_forward, 4=outgoing_cltv_value, 6=short_channel_id (L194-205). HMAC is 32 bytes, checked by the next hop. Correct.
- **C10** `5.0-onion-routing-101.md:37` · crypto · ✅ correct
    - claim: "each forwarder strips one layer off the entire buffer, exposing its own hop payload at the front while the inner layers still cover the rest."
    - evidence: BOLT 4 L940-952: XOR rho over the whole hop_payloads buffer, then remove length+payload+32-byte next_hmac from the FRONT. One XOR pass over the entire buffer; current payload emerges at front, deeper layers remain encrypted. Correct.
- **C12** `5.0-onion-routing-101.md:39` · crypto · ✅ correct
    - claim: "Before decrypting anything, each hop recomputes this tag over the payload ... and checks it"
    - evidence: BOLT 4 processing order: derive mu + compute/compare HMAC (L935-939) comes BEFORE deriving rho and XOR-decrypting (L940-942). 'Before decrypting anything' ordering is correct per spec.
- **C13** `5.0-onion-routing-101.md:45` · crypto · ✅ correct
    - claim: "The innermost layer is peeled last, so it has to be added first ... Alice builds each layer on top of the prior one, working from the inside out!"
    - evidence: BOLT 4 construction L862-893 iterates hops from the last (final) hop backward; nextHmac begins all-zero for the final hop and each outer HMAC is computed over the already-built inner buffer. Inside-out construction = Dave first, Bob last. Correct.
- **C14** `5.0-onion-routing-101.md:47` · crypto · ✅ correct
    - claim: "each hop's HMAC is computed over the encrypted layer beneath it, so an inner layer has to exist before Alice can authenticate the layer wrapped around it."
    - evidence: BOLT 4 L810-816 + L862-893: each next HMAC computed (with mu-key) over the current packet state, which already contains the inner layers; final HMAC is for the first hop. Nesting forces inside-out build. Correct.
- **C15** `5.0-onion-routing-101.md:49` · numeric · ✅ correct
    - claim: "the original padding is 1,300 bytes"
    - evidence: BOLT 4 L144,159,165 (1300-byte hop_payloads) and L787 ('packet is initialized with 1300 random bytes'). Cross-checked ch7 L5 ('Payload: 1,300-bytes'). Correct.
- **C16** `5.0-onion-routing-101.md:53` · numeric · ✅ correct
    - claim: "Alice has a 1,300-byte payload area with three nested encryption layers. She appends an outer HMAC (bob_hmac), since Bob is the first recipient"
    - evidence: 3-hop path Alice->Bob->Charlie->Dave => 3 hop payloads => 3 nested layers within the 1300-byte hop_payloads. BOLT 4 L813-816: final HMAC (computed last) is the one used by the first hop (Bob). Correct.
- **C17** `5.0-onion-routing-101.md:63-65` · crypto · ✅ correct
    - claim: "Verify the outer HMAC ... If they don't match, they drop the packet. Decrypt with XOR ... Read the hop payload at the front ... extract the next-hop's HMAC ... construct the new 1,300-byte packet"
    - evidence: BOLT 4 L936-961 in exact order: compute/compare HMAC -> abort if differ -> XOR with rho -> remove length+payload -> remove 32-byte next_hmac -> forward hop_payloads truncated to 1300 with hmac=next_hmac. Matches the three steps. Correct.
- **C18** `5.0-onion-routing-101.md:71` · crypto · ✅ correct
    - claim: "the encryption layer comes off the entire payload, not just the current hop's payload ... when Bob XORs his payload, it reveals his plaintext TLV, but Charlie's and Dave's are still encrypted within deeper layers."
    - evidence: BOLT 4 L940-942: single XOR of rho over entire hop_payloads buffer. Only the front (current hop) payload becomes plaintext; remaining bytes are still under the inner hops' rho layers (Alice applied one rho layer per hop during construction). Adversarial check: Bob holds the full 1300-byte buffer and can left-shift/insp
- **C19** `5.0-onion-routing-101.md:73` · crypto · ✅ correct
    - claim: "When the packet finally reaches Dave, his hop payload's HMAC field contains 32 zero bytes. Per BOLT 4, an all-zero next-hop HMAC signals that the receiving node is the final destination"
    - evidence: BOLT 4 L955 ('If next_hmac is not all-zero (not the final node)') and L964-965 ('Otherwise (all-zero next_hmac): This is the final destination of the onion'). Construction L862 sets initial nextHmac = [32]byte{} (zeros) for the final hop. Correct.
- **C20** `5.0-onion-routing-101.md:81` · crypto · ✅ correct
    - claim: "The packet's outer HMAC is bob_hmac. Since this is the last HMAC Alice derives when creating the onion, it commits to all other payload data within the onion."
    - evidence: BOLT 4 L810-816: 'The resulting final HMAC value is the HMAC that will be used by the first hop.' Built last over the fully-wrapped buffer, so it commits to everything beneath. Correct.
- **C21** `5.0-onion-routing-101.md:82-84` · crypto · ✅ correct
    - claim: "Inside Bob's hop payload sits charlie_hmac ... Inside Charlie's hop payload sits dave_hmac ... Inside Dave's hop payload, the HMAC field is 0x00... (32 zeros)"
    - evidence: Each hop payload carries the NEXT hop's HMAC (BOLT 4 L171, L952 'Remove 32 bytes as next_hmac'). For Alice->Bob->Charlie->Dave: Bob's payload holds Charlie's hmac, Charlie's holds Dave's hmac, Dave's holds all-zero (final). Consistent with C19. Correct.
- **C22** `5.0-onion-routing-101.md:86` · crypto · ✅ correct
    - claim: "Each one commits to everything below it: the hop payload, the next-inner HMAC, and all the encrypted layers underneath."
    - evidence: BOLT 4 L178-180: 'payload is protected under the packet-wide HMAC ... fully authenticated'; construction computes each HMAC over the buffer that already contains inner layers. Nested commitment is correct.
- **C23** `5.0-onion-routing-101.md:96` · numeric · ✅ correct
    - claim: "digging into each of the five keys that the Sphinx protocol uses."
    - evidence: BOLT 4 Key Generation L108-113 lists rho, mu, um, pad (four); the error section adds 'ammag' (L1070) as the return-encryption key. Total of five core keys (rho/mu/um/ammag/pad) is exactly the framing chapter 6 uses (6.0-key-derivation.md L35 'five core operations', L50 'Four labels (rho, mu, um, ammag)... The fifth lab
- **C24** `5.0-onion-routing-101.md:94` · crypto · ✅ correct
    - claim: "If we reused one raw secret for all of the encryption and authentication jobs, we'd be opening ourselves up to some pretty bad attack vectors."
    - evidence: BOLT 4 derives distinct keys (rho/mu/um/pad/ammag) from the shared secret via HMAC256 with different labels (L115-122), precisely to avoid key reuse across encryption vs authentication. Consistent with ch6 L26-32 rationale. Correct.

- **C2** `6.0-key-derivation.md:20` · crypto · ✅ correct

- **C3** `6.0-key-derivation.md:21` · crypto · ✅ correct
    - claim: "Authenticate the forward layer with a message authentication code (MAC) (HMAC-SHA256) ... so the forwarder can detect tampering *before* processing."
    - evidence: mu is the forward HMAC key (BOLT4:110 'used during the HMAC generation'). HMAC check-before-decrypt is the standard processing order (the hmac authenticates the packet, BOLT4:146). Matches chapter's line-57 'checks it first, before decrypting'.
- **C4** `6.0-key-derivation.md:22` · crypto · ✅ correct
    - claim: "Encrypt return-path errors with a stream cipher so only Alice can read the failure reason."
    - evidence: ammag is the return-path stream-cipher (ChaCha20) key applied via XOR (BOLT4:1070-1072). Each return hop re-wraps with its own ammag; only Alice holds all hops' ammag keys to peel.
- **C5** `6.0-key-derivation.md:23` · crypto · ✅ correct
    - claim: "Authenticate return-path errors with a MAC so Alice can verify the error actually came from a specific hop on her route."
    - evidence: um is the return HMAC key: BOLT4:1066-1068 'hmac ... with a key generated ... with key type um'. Confirmed um_key=4da7f2923edce6... for hop[4] in onion-error-test.json.
- **C6** `6.0-key-derivation.md:24` · crypto · ✅ correct
    - claim: "Initialize the empty buffer with a stream cipher so unused space at the end of the packet doesn't leak path length."
    - evidence: pad key seeds a ChaCha20 stream to pre-fill the 1300-byte buffer: BOLT4:787-792 'initialized with 1300 random bytes ... The pad key ... ChaCha20 ... generate 1300 random bytes ... starting state of the mix-header.' BOLT4:112 'random filler bytes for the starting mix-header packet'.
- **C7** `6.0-key-derivation.md:30` · crypto · ✅ correct
    - claim: "BOLT 4 uses ChaCha20 with the same nonce (zero) everywhere, including for both forward and backward encryption. This is safe only because every operation gets its own key: the spec notes that *"the use of a fixed nonce is safe, since the keys are never reused."*"
    - evidence: BOLT4:131-135: streams use ChaCha20 with a 96-bit zero-nonce, and verbatim 'The use of a fixed nonce is safe, since the keys are never reused.' The same byte-stream method (zero nonce) governs both forward (rho) and backward (ammag) per BOLT4:1146 ('identical to the obfuscation steps the erring node carries out').
- **C8** `6.0-key-derivation.md:30` · crypto · ✅ correct
    - claim: "If forward and backward encryption shared a key, an attacker could XOR the forward and backward payload ciphertexts together and potentially recover the original plaintext."
    - evidence: Standard two-time-pad attack: with a stream cipher under a fixed (zero) nonce, two ciphertexts C1=P1 XOR KS and C2=P2 XOR KS share keystream KS, so C1 XOR C2 = P1 XOR P2, removing the key and leaking plaintext relationships. The spec's safety rests precisely on per-operation keys (BOLT4:135). Correct as a 'potentially 
- **C9** `6.0-key-derivation.md:42` · formula · ✅ correct
    - claim: "generate_key(name, secret) = HMAC-SHA256(key=name, msg=secret)"
    - evidence: BOLT4:119-122: 'Keys are generated by computing an HMAC (with SHA256 ...) using the appropriate key-type ... as HMAC-key and the 32-byte shared secret as the message.' Matches python-snippet 'generate-key' (PythonSnippet.tsx:85) hmac.new(name.encode(), secret, hashlib.sha256).digest().
- **C10** `6.0-key-derivation.md:48` · crypto · ✅ correct
    - claim: "the output of this function will be another 32-byte pseudorandom value ... by using standardized names, the derivation becomes deterministic and both Alice and each subsequent hop can derive the exact same keys from the same shared secret."
    - evidence: HMAC-SHA256 output is 32 bytes (BOLT4:116-117 'returns a 32-byte key'). Determinism: same (label, shared_secret) -> same HMAC, and both Alice and the hop share ss_i (ECDH), so both derive identical keys. Reproduced all four labels from ss=53eb63... and they match onion-error-test.json (ammag) exactly.
- **C11** `6.0-key-derivation.md:50` · crypto · ✅ correct
    - claim: "Four labels (`rho`, `mu`, `um`, and `ammag`) are used with each hop's shared secret ss_i, making them unique to that hop. The fifth label (`pad`) is used with Alice's session key."
    - evidence: rho/mu/um/ammag derive from the per-hop shared secret (BOLT4:106-111, 1070; per-hop ammag_key/um_key confirmed in onion-error-test.json). pad derives from sessionKey (BOLT4:866). Internally consistent with line 3 and 62.
- **C12** `6.0-key-derivation.md:56` · crypto · ✅ correct
    - claim: "**`rho`**: the forward encryption key. A ChaCha20 stream-cipher key. ... One key both ways, because XOR-ing twice with the same keystream cancels out."
    - evidence: rho = obfuscation/stream key (BOLT4:108-109). XOR is involutive: (P XOR KS) XOR KS = P, so Alice's encrypt and the forwarder's strip use the same rho keystream. Correct.
- **C13** `6.0-key-derivation.md:57` · crypto · ✅ correct
    - claim: "**`mu`**: the forward authentication key. An HMAC key. ... the forwarder recomputes that tag and checks it *first*, before decrypting anything."
    - evidence: mu = HMAC key (BOLT4:110). The 32-byte packet hmac authenticates integrity (BOLT4:146); check-then-process is the standard order so a forwarder rejects tampered packets before acting.
- **C14** `6.0-key-derivation.md:58` · crypto · ✅ correct
    - claim: "**`um`**: the return authentication key. An HMAC key. A hop that fails signs its error with `um`; Alice later recomputes the tag with the same key."
    - evidence: BOLT4:1066-1068 error-packet hmac uses key type um. um_key=4da7f2923edce6c2... confirmed for the erring hop[4] in onion-error-test.json. um is mu reversed (return-direction MAC).
- **C15** `6.0-key-derivation.md:59` · crypto · ✅ correct
    - claim: "**`ammag`**: the return encryption key. A ChaCha20 stream-cipher key. The failing hop (and each hop on the way back) XORs the error with `ammag`'s keystream to wrap it."
    - evidence: BOLT4:1070-1072 erring node generates ammag key -> pseudo-random stream applied via XOR; BOLT4:1146 each forwarding hop re-applies its own ammag. Per-hop ammag_key values present for all 5 hops in onion-error-test.json and reproduced exactly (hop0 ammag=3761ba4d3e726d8a...).
- **C16** `6.0-key-derivation.md:60` · crypto · ✅ correct
    - claim: "**`pad`**: the buffer-setup key. Derived from Alice's session key (not a per-hop secret). Alice alone uses it, once, to pre-fill the empty payload area."
    - evidence: BOLT4:787-792 + 866: pad/paddingKey from sessionKey, used once by the origin to seed the 1300-byte starting buffer. Hops never derive pad. Consistent with line 62.
- **C17** `6.0-key-derivation.md:62` · crypto · ✅ correct
    - claim: "each hop has its own `rho`, `mu`, `um`, and `ammag` key ... The `pad` key is different: Alice derives it from the session key once while building the packet."
    - evidence: Same as C11/C16; per-hop derivation confirmed by distinct per-hop ammag_key/um_key in onion-error-test.json; pad from session key (BOLT4:866). Internally consistent.
- **C18** `6.0-key-derivation.md:64` · glossary · ✅ correct

    - evidence: Label byte-checks: 'ammag' reversed = 'gamma'; 'um' reversed = 'mu'. rho/mu correspond to the Sphinx rho (stream) and mu (MAC) oracles, consistent with BOLT4:108-110 roles. Etymology aside, internally consistent and accurate.
- **C19** `6.0-key-derivation.md:75` · crypto · ✅ correct

- **C1** `7.0-fixed-size-and-filler.md:3-6` · numeric · ✅ correct
    - claim: "every onion packet is 1,366 bytes ... Header: 34 bytes: 1-byte version, and 33-byte ephemeral pubkey; Payload: 1,300-bytes ...; HMAC: 32-bytes"
    - evidence: BOLT4 bolt04.md:141-160: version(1)+public_key(33)+hop_payloads(1300)+hmac(32). 1+33=34 header, +1300+32=1366 total. Matches.
- **C2** `7.0-fixed-size-and-filler.md:20` · numeric · ✅ correct
    - claim: "Bob, the first hop, receives a 306-byte packet and peels his 60-byte hop payload off the front. Then, he forwards the next 246-byte onion packet to Charlie. Charlie peels his 80-byte payload and forwards the next 166-byte onion packet to Dave."
    - evidence: Strawman (no-fixed-size) arithmetic. Envelope=1+33+32=66. Payloads 60+80+100=240. 66+240=306. 306-60=246. 246-80=166. 166-100=66. All internally consistent with the example 60/80/100 sizes.
- **C3** `7.0-fixed-size-and-filler.md:24` · crypto · ✅ correct
    - claim: "intermediate hops should not know where they are in the path. This rule is breaking right in front of our eyes!"
    - evidence: Adversarial: a shrinking packet leaks DOWNSTREAM hops remaining (size proportional to remaining payloads), i.e. distance-to-destination/positional info. It does not leak absolute upstream position, but the educational claim 'know where they are in the path' is a fair reading of a positional leak. Consistent with prompt
- **C4** `7.0-fixed-size-and-filler.md:28` · numeric · ✅ correct
    - claim: "the Lightning Network uses the Sphinx packet format, which fixes the size of each onion packet at exactly 1,366 bytes for every hop"
    - evidence: BOLT4 bolt04.md:782 'returns a single 1366-byte packet'; fixed size for every hop (forward truncates to 1300 hop_payloads, §960). Matches.
- **C5** `7.0-fixed-size-and-filler.md:30` · formula · ✅ correct
    - claim: "he shifts the inner contents forward to fill the front gap, and then fills the new gap at the back of the buffer with bytes, called "padding""
    - evidence: BOLT4 bolt04.md:975 'deobfuscating and left-shifting the field'; §977 'the field is pre-padded before forwarding'. The removed front payload creates a back gap filled by deterministic filler. Matches.
- **C6** `7.0-fixed-size-and-filler.md:34` · crypto · ✅ correct
    - claim: "The bytes must be indistinguishable from the encrypted hop payloads that came before. If they're not, then a forwarder could still tell where the "real" content ends and the "padding" begins"
    - evidence: BOLT4 bolt04.md:988-989 the XOR 'while simultaneously obfuscating the added 0x00-bytes at the end' — padding is rho-obfuscated so it is ciphertext-indistinguishable. A distinguishable boundary would re-leak route length. Reasoning sound.
- **C7** `7.0-fixed-size-and-filler.md:35` · crypto · ✅ correct
    - claim: "before a forwarder does anything, it recomputes the HMAC over the exact bytes it received and drops the packet if the result doesn't match the HMAC in the packet"
    - evidence: BOLT4 bolt04.md:935-939: derive mu, HMAC over hop_payloads||associated_data, constant-time compare, abort if differ — done BEFORE rho-decryption (§940). 'before a forwarder does anything' is accurate re: before decrypting. Matches.
- **C8** `7.0-fixed-size-and-filler.md:37` · crypto · ✅ correct
    - claim: "that would invalidate Charlie's HMAC, which Alice computed when building the onion using her shared secret with Charlie"
    - evidence: BOLT4 bolt04.md:810-811 next HMAC computed with mu-key over hop_payloads; mu=HMAC256("mu",ss) where ss is Alice<->Charlie shared secret. Wrong back-padding changes hop_payloads and breaks the HMAC. Matches.
- **C9** `7.0-fixed-size-and-filler.md:54` · crypto · ✅ correct
    - claim: "derive his keys, verify the HMAC, prepare the buffer, XOR the whole thing in a single pass, slice off his hop payload from the front, and then fill in the gap before forwarding the next 1,366-byte packet"
    - evidence: Ordering matches BOLT4 bolt04.md:934-961: derive ss->mu, verify HMAC (935-939), derive rho (940), XOR over 2x buffer (941-942), strip front payload (943-952), forward (957-961). Forwarded packet is again 1366 bytes. Matches.
- **C10** `7.0-fixed-size-and-filler.md:58` · numeric · ✅ correct
    - claim: "he does it all in one XOR pass over a 2,600-byte buffer ... it pads the 1,300-byte hop_payloads area with 1,300 zero bytes to reach 2 × ROUTING_INFO_SIZE = 2,600 bytes and XORs the whole thing against chacha20(rho_B, 2600)"
    - evidence: BOLT4 bolt04.md:984-987 'pads it with 1300 0x00-bytes, such that the total length is 2*1300' then XORs a stream of matching length. §941 'bytestream of twice the length of hop_payloads'. 2*1300=2600. Matches exactly.
- **C11** `7.0-fixed-size-and-filler.md:60-62` · crypto · ✅ correct
    - claim: "Decrypts Bob's hop payload at the front (the first 60 bytes become plaintext). Peels one of Alice's encryption layers off the downstream payloads and the padding. Produces 60 brand-new bytes at the back, which is the exact same bytes that Alice used when calculating the HMAC."
    - evidence: Single XOR with rho_B over (hop_payloads||1300 zeros): front 60 bytes (bigsize+payload+hmac for s_B=60) decrypt, inner layers peel one layer, and (zeros XOR rho_B[1300..1359]) = the deterministic filler Alice pre-generated. Consistent with BOLT4 bolt04.md:988-989 and filler reasoning.
- **C13** `7.0-fixed-size-and-filler.md:66` · formula · ✅ correct
    - claim: "a left-shift by Bob's hop-payload size (his bytes are gone from the front; the remaining content moves up; new bytes are added at the back)"
    - evidence: BOLT4 bolt04.md:975 describes extraction as 'left-shifting the field'. Net effect of removing s_B front bytes + appending s_B back filler = left-shift by s_B. Matches.
- **C14** `7.0-fixed-size-and-filler.md:76` · formula · ✅ correct
    - claim: "Alice ... appends 60 zero bytes (step 2), generates Bob's full 1,360-byte rho_B keystream (step 3), slices off just its trailing 60 bytes (step 4), and XORs the two together (step 5). That is Bob's slice of the filler."
    - evidence: For s_B=60: keystream length 1300+60=1360; trailing 60 bytes = positions 1300..1359; XOR with 60 zeros gives rho_B[1300..1359]. These are exactly the bytes Bob regenerates at peel (positions 1300..1359 of his 2600-XOR), since chacha20 keystream[0:1360] is a prefix of keystream[0:2600]. Consistent with BOLT4 filler algo
- **C15** `7.0-fixed-size-and-filler.md:77` · numeric · ✅ correct
    - claim: "The bytes at positions 1,300 through 1,359 of his result (zeros ⊕ rho_B[1,300..1,359]) become the back of the 1,300-byte payload area he forwards to Charlie."
    - evidence: Positions 1300..1359 = 60 bytes (1359-1300+1=60=s_B). In the forwarded region (positions 60..1359), these are the LAST 60 bytes = the back. Correctly states 1,300-byte payload area (consistent with BOLT4 §960 and contradicts the looser line 64). Matches.
- **C16** `7.0-fixed-size-and-filler.md:79` · crypto · ✅ correct
    - claim: "It is the same zeros ⊕ rho_B[1,300..1,359] both times, because Alice and Bob share rho_B (each derives it from ss_AB, their ECDH shared secret)."
    - evidence: BOLT4 bolt04.md:940 rho=HMAC256("rho",ss); §934 ss=ECDH(public_key,node_privkey). Alice computes the identical ss via her session key and Bob's pubkey, so identical rho_B, identical keystream positions -> identical bytes. Matches.
- **C17** `7.0-fixed-size-and-filler.md:85` · crypto · ✅ correct
    - claim: "Alice has to handle Bob's shift (which affects what Charlie sees as his last s_B bytes ...) and Charlie's shift (which affects what Dave sees as his last s_C bytes ...). Dave doesn't shift anything (he's the final hop), so no filler is generated for the final hop."
    - evidence: Forwarders are Bob and Charlie only (Dave is destination). BOLT4 bolt04.md:1011 loop runs numHops-1 times; §1035 'last hop need not obfuscate the filler'. Bob's s_B new back-bytes become Charlie's last s_B bytes; Charlie's s_C become Dave's last s_C bytes. Matches.
- **C18** `7.0-fixed-size-and-filler.md:97` · formula · ✅ correct
    - claim: "Alice generates Bob's rho keystream, extended to cover both the original 1,300-byte hop_payloads area and s_B extra bytes past it (so 1,300 + s_B bytes total) ... Alice XORs the last s_B bytes of the 1,300 + s_B keystream into the filler."
    - evidence: After step 2 filler length = s_B. Last s_B bytes of a (1300+s_B)-byte keystream = positions 1300..(1300+s_B-1) = Bob's back-generated filler positions. Matches the peel-time bytes (C14/C15) and BOLT4 reference algorithm.
- **C19** `7.0-fixed-size-and-filler.md:105` · formula · ✅ correct
    - claim: "the filler has length s_B + s_C: the first s_B bytes still hold Bob's keystream extension from step 2, and the new s_C zero bytes are placeholders ... (which will end up as the last s_C bytes of Dave's view)"
    - evidence: Append s_C zeros to an s_B-length filler -> s_B+s_C total. Charlie's new back bytes (s_C) become the last s_C bytes Dave receives. Consistent with the incremental-filler invariant in BOLT4 bolt04.md:1006-1030.
- **C20** `7.0-fixed-size-and-filler.md:109` · formula · ✅ correct
    - claim: "Alice generates Charlie's rho keystream extended to cover 1,300 + s_C bytes, and XORs the last s_B + s_C bytes of that keystream into the filler. Because the filler is now s_B + s_C bytes long, the s_B + s_C bytes of keystream ... overlap Charlie's regular 1,300-byte region by s_"
    - evidence: Last s_B+s_C bytes of a (1300+s_C)-byte keystream = positions (1300-s_B)..(1300+s_C-1). Intersection with Charlie's 0..1299 region = (1300-s_B)..1299 = s_B bytes. So the s_B-byte overlap into the regular region is exactly where Bob's accumulated filler sits at Charlie's peel — matching the LND-style incremental filler 
- **C21** `7.0-fixed-size-and-filler.md:113-115` · crypto · ✅ correct
    - claim: "Dave is the final hop. Since he doesn't forward the packet, Alice doesn't have to add any filler bytes; there is no next recipient who needs to verify an HMAC."
    - evidence: BOLT4 bolt04.md:1035-1036 'The last hop need not obfuscate the filler, since it won't forward the packet ... and thus need not extract an HMAC either.' Matches.
- **C22** `7.0-fixed-size-and-filler.md:123` · code · ✅ correct
    - claim: "you'll write OnionPacketBuilder.generate_filler, which takes the route's rho keys and the hop payload sizes for the forwarder hops, and produces the filler bytes Alice writes into the packet during construction"
    - evidence: Consistent with the prose algorithm: filler is built from each forwarder's rho key and hop-payload size (forwarders Bob+Charlie, not Dave). Not auditing the exercise code body (out of scope), but the prose description is accurate to the algorithm above.
- **C23** `7.0-fixed-size-and-filler.md:3` · consistency · ✅ correct
    - claim: "In chapter 5, Onion Routing 101, we saw that every onion packet is 1,366 bytes"
    - evidence: Cross-checked 5.0-onion-routing-101.md:5 'making every packet exactly 1,366 bytes' and :53/:65 '1,300-byte payload area'. The chapter-5 reference and the 1,366/1,300 figures are consistent. No drift.

    - claim: "One XOR strips Bob layer from every byte, and his hop payload turns plaintext at the front."
    - evidence: BOLT4:986-989 one XOR of the 2600-extended buffer deobfuscates this hop and re-obfuscates appended zeros into regenerated filler.

    - evidence: BOLT4:808-809,888-893 last hop overwrites tail with filler then computes HMAC; 118B=FILLER_B; innermost = dave (scenes.ts:445).

### visual WrapPrimerDiagram.tsx  ·  20 claims · 3 flagged
_Coverage:_ Read the entire file (1250 lines) and the relevant BOLT 4 sections (Packet Structure, Key Generation, Packet Construction lines 748-818, Onion Decryption 935-965, Filler Generation 971-994) plus BOLT 1 BigSize (lines 587-605) and the onion-test.json worked vector. - **C2** `client/src/components/onion-routing-draft/WrapPrimerDiagram.tsx:914-916` · formula · ❌ INCORRECT **[Low]**
    - claim: "For hop payloads ≤252 bytes, that's a single byte equal to (slot_size - 1)."
    - evidence: The rendered LEN values use slot_size-33 (27,47,67), not slot_size-1 (which would be 59,79,99 = 0x3B/0x4F/0x63). BOLT 4 line 100-101 confirms the bigsize excludes both the 1-byte prefix and the 32-byte trailing HMAC. The correct comment at lines 643-644 already says 'slot total minus the 1-byte bigsize prefix and the t
    - should be: Should read '(slot_size - 33)' i.e. slot_size minus the 1-byte bigsize prefix and the 32-byte HMAC field. (Also: the single-byte bigsize applies when the encoded length value is <253, i.e. slot_size<286, not literally 'hop payloads ≤252 bytes'.)
